  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7376fd1f-2c1e-41e4-bad6-db692a030dab'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2562318373818444850">There are a few things Jeremy Marsh was sure he’d never do: he’d never leave New York City; never give his heart away after barely surviving one failed marriage; and never become a parent. Now Jeremy is living in the tiny town of Boone Creek, North Carolina, engaged to Lexie Darnell, the love of his life, and anticipating the start of their family. But just as his life see</span>
  <span id="freeText2562318373818444850" style="display:none">There are a few things Jeremy Marsh was sure he’d never do: he’d never leave New York City; never give his heart away after barely surviving one failed marriage; and never become a parent. Now Jeremy is living in the tiny town of Boone Creek, North Carolina, engaged to Lexie Darnell, the love of his life, and anticipating the start of their family. But just as his life seems to be settling into a blissful pattern, a mysterious and disturbing e-mail sets off a chain of events that will change the course of this young couple’s relationship. How well do we really know the ones we love? How do we handle the inevitable doubts, fears concerning parenthood, and stumbling blocks that are sometimes placed in our way? Continuing the story of the young couple introduced in Sparks’s bestselling True Believer, this novel captures all the heartbreak, tension, romance and surprises of those who are newly wed. An astonishing tale about the love between a man and a woman and between a parent and a child, At First Sight is about endings that bring new beginnings . . . tragedies that lead to unexpected joy . . . and, most of all, the magic of everlasting love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2562318373818444850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I would have read it at 14. I read Rebecca at that age and this book has similar moral values. She should read True Believers first though. At First S<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I would have read it at 14. I read Rebecca at that age and this book has similar moral values. She should read True Believers first though. At First Sight is somewhat sad at the end, so your daughter may be saddened and need to talk. You're view of death (in childbirth) will determine how she'd handle the book. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13365319027057673124">At First Sight (Jeremy Marsh & Lexie Darnell, #2), Nicholas Sparks<br/><br/>At First Sight is a romance novel by Nicholas Sparks, written in 2005. Set in North Carolina, United States, At First Sight is the sequel to Sparks’ previous book, "True Believer", written in the same year. At First Sight, was originally the result of a 45-page epilogue in True Believer. Sparks’ editor thought this was too long for an epilogue, and damaged the effect of True Believer. It was then that Sparks got the idea to write </span>
  <span id="freeText13365319027057673124" style="display:none">At First Sight (Jeremy Marsh &amp; Lexie Darnell, #2), Nicholas Sparks<br /><br />At First Sight is a romance novel by Nicholas Sparks, written in 2005. Set in North Carolina, United States, At First Sight is the sequel to Sparks’ previous book, "True Believer", written in the same year. At First Sight, was originally the result of a 45-page epilogue in True Believer. Sparks’ editor thought this was too long for an epilogue, and damaged the effect of True Believer. It was then that Sparks got the idea to write "At First Sight" as its predecessor.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: هشتم ماه فوریه سال 2008 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: در اولین نگاه؛ نویسنده: نیکلاس اسپارکس؛ مترجم: شهرزاد فتوحی؛ مشخصات نشر تهران، پاینده، 1386، در 336 ص، شابک 9789642950003؛ چاپ دوم 1392؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 21م<br /> <br />عنوان: در اولین نگاه؛ نویسنده: نیکلاس اسپارکس؛ مترجم نفیسه معتکف؛ مشخصات نشر تهران، درسا، 1386، در 370ص، شابک 9789648759358؛ <br /><br />در اولین نگاه؛ داستانی مستقل و در عین حال ادامه ی داستان «باورم کن»؛ اثر همین نویسنده است؛ «جرمی» سی و هفت ساله، برای ماموریتی از نیویورک، به «بون کریک» میرود، و در آنجا «در اولین نگاه»، عاشق «لکسی» میشود؛ بارداری «لکسی»، آغاز ارسال ایمیلهایی مرموز، و توصیه های مادر بزرگ «لکسی»، که واسطه ی روحی است، همه دست به دست هم میدهند تا «جرمی» با مشکلاتی مواجه شود؛ ...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_42531432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42531432" />
    <a title="treehugger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/123501-treehugger"><img alt="treehugger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181356993p2/123501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42531432?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="treehugger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="treehugger" href="/user/show/123501-treehugger">treehugger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781586216986" href="/book/show/263658.At_First_Sight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/123501-treehugger?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/123501-treehugger?shelf=read_2009">read_2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/123501-treehugger?shelf=north-carolina">north-carolina</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/123501-treehugger?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42531432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8914437623355817073">Ok, usually I really like Sparks - his books are enjoyable, quick reads that don't take too many brain cells and sometimes give you a few warm fuzzies.<br/><br/>Now, I didn't put this together with "True Believer" until I started to write this review, so I was pissed throughout the entire book because there was NO detail about how they fell in love, so it was completely unbelievable - it sounded like Jeremy was constantly trying to talk himself into believing he was in love. <br/><br/>I was listening to this one in</span>
  <span id="freeText8914437623355817073" style="display:none">Ok, usually I really like Sparks - his books are enjoyable, quick reads that don't take too many brain cells and sometimes give you a few warm fuzzies.<br /><br />Now, I didn't put this together with "True Believer" until I started to write this review, so I was pissed throughout the entire book because there was NO detail about how they fell in love, so it was completely unbelievable - it sounded like Jeremy was constantly trying to talk himself into believing he was in love. <br /><br />I was listening to this one in the car and honestly only finished it to continue screaming obscenities every few minutes because of the absurdity of some of the dialogue and the idiocy of the characters. I mean..the characters were super dumb. Dense. IQ impaired. Which made me not like them.<br /><br />And the narrator had the creepiest fake Southern accented falsetto when he did Lexie's voice that he made her sound even less intelligent than some of her dialogue. <br /><br />Truly this was a groundbreakingly terrible novel! I think it deserves some kind of award...Sparks might be running out of steam, because this novel was pure drivel. <br /><br />And if I had more free time on my hands I'd write him a letter to tell him how much I didn't appreciate the ridiculous number of "way down south" stereotypes that he put into Boone Creek - I've lived in NC for a long time, and I've never met anyone named Jed, I don't know any taxidermists who only grunt instead of speaking (and are ordained ministers as a side job?? - ok, I don't know any taxidermists PERIOD), NONE of the men I know dress in flannel shirts, and I've NEVER heard of a mayor who is so very involved in the personal lives of the (not wealthy) people in his town! I mean, this stuff was RIDICULOUS. RE-DIC-U-LUSS.<br /><br />Don't read this. Please. For me. Don't read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8914437623355817073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3263582683225101172">I only ever pick up Nicholas Sparks because I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15931.The_Notebook__The_Notebook___1_' title='The Notebook (The Notebook, #1) by Nicholas Sparks' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Notebook</a>, but this time it was a mistake. The three main events in the book are:<br/>1. Jeremy and Lexie are getting married, but someone is trying to break them up. <br/>2. Their baby could die or be born with a deformity. <br/>3. Ta-da!   <span id="freeText3263582683225101172" style="display:none">I only ever pick up Nicholas Sparks because I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15931.The_Notebook__The_Notebook___1_" title="The Notebook (The Notebook, #1) by Nicholas Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Notebook</a>, but this time it was a mistake. The three main events in the book are:<br />1. Jeremy and Lexie are getting married, but someone is trying to break them up. <br />2. Their baby could die or be born with a deformity. <br />3. Ta-da! Neither of those happen! Lexie just dies in childbirth instead. But her death had nothing to do with the the threats to their relationship or the disease the baby didn't get, it was just a freak accident. So by the end, the story seemed totally disjointed, like he's just throwing in anything tragic to keep the women of America in tears. Badly done sir, badly done indeed.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780751536577" href="/book/show/589134.At_First_Sight">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Dana by: </span>
      Anu! Can I puhleeez kill you!? x)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4421337-dana?shelf=love">love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4421337-dana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262296253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8751921014680033702">After reading many Nicholas Sparks books, I thought that he lost his magic. I no longer cried for any of his books and my rating lessened to 3-4 stars. So, when I first saw this book, it had 'boredom' written all over it. But little did I know that this book was that "tear-trigger" of a book!! The guy is wicked! He made me cry. Uncontrollably! I mean how could he do this!? I thought this book was gonna end with a happy note just like True Believer (its first part!). But here I'm crying like neve</span>
  <span id="freeText8751921014680033702" style="display:none">After reading many Nicholas Sparks books, I thought that he lost his magic. I no longer cried for any of his books and my rating lessened to 3-4 stars. So, when I first saw this book, it had 'boredom' written all over it. But little did I know that this book was that "tear-trigger" of a book!! The guy is wicked! He made me cry. Uncontrollably! I mean how could he do this!? I thought this book was gonna end with a happy note just like True Believer (its first part!). But here I'm crying like never before. Why!? Why her? And I would like to slap that one-heck-of-a-jerk Alvin! All I can say is that I cried and cried wondering to myself "What the fish is wrong with me! It's just a book! You are not Jeremy, you don't know Lexie and you haven't seen Claire"! Beautiful, sad, eye-roller...the book is wow. I know it's a cliche. He has a killed a lot of his characters and left lot of the lovers crying. But, I don't know, this book just got through ma heart not even waiting for its pass to be checked!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8751921014680033702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1257515929795472881">Nicholas Sparks brings back the characters first introduced in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13152679.True_Believers' title='True Believers by Kurt Andersen' rel='nofollow noopener'>True Believer</a> - Jeremy Marsh, a writer from New York City; and Lexie Darnell, the small-town, southern librarian. In <i>At First Sight</i>, Jeremy and Lexie are preparing for their upcoming wedding shortly after Jeremy's move down to Boone Creek, N.C. to be with her. On top of the wedding stress, the couple is also trying to keep it under wraps that Lexie is pregnant.<br/><br/>The book follows Jeremy and Lexie through the pregnancy, the subsequent pu</span>
  <span id="freeText1257515929795472881" style="display:none">Nicholas Sparks brings back the characters first introduced in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13152679.True_Believers" title="True Believers by Kurt Andersen" rel="nofollow noopener">True Believer</a> - Jeremy Marsh, a writer from New York City; and Lexie Darnell, the small-town, southern librarian. In <i>At First Sight</i>, Jeremy and Lexie are preparing for their upcoming wedding shortly after Jeremy's move down to Boone Creek, N.C. to be with her. On top of the wedding stress, the couple is also trying to keep it under wraps that Lexie is pregnant.<br /><br />The book follows Jeremy and Lexie through the pregnancy, the subsequent purchase of a house, and Jeremy's writer's block that doesn't seem to be going away. When Jeremy begins to receive suspicious emails from an anonymous sender, the relationship goes through more twists and turns.<br /><br />Sparks rounds the book out with former characters: Lexie's psychic grandmother, the mayor of Boone Creek who always seems to know everyone's business, and the taxidermist/hotel employee whose wedding gift is a stuffed wild boar. The quirks and predicaments will keep readers laughing, but the subsequent happenings in the story make this book as much of a tearjerker as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15931.The_Notebook__The_Notebook___1_" title="The Notebook (The Notebook, #1) by Nicholas Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Notebook</a>. Sparks has a wonderful grip on the relationships between men and women, and just how many boundaries true love can cross. Can one fall in love at first sight? Read and find out...</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_95857002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95857002" />
    <a title="Rhiannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3407931-rhiannon"><img alt="Rhiannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310618784p2/3407931.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95857002?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhiannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhiannon" href="/user/show/3407931-rhiannon">Rhiannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer95857002&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95857002" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16063942680760630592">Horrible book! I didn't know Sparks had it in him. I usually love his novels...they're easy, feel-good reads. But this one, ulgh, where do I start?<br/><br/>The characters (especially Lexie) were SO annoying through the whole thing. Lexie wasn't willing to sacrifice anything to be with Jeremy...he had to move to Boone Creek, in the middle of nowhere, and do everything else on her terms. Bought the house she wanted, the renovations she wanted, in the city she wanted etc...and meanwhile, she didn't even see</span>
  <span id="freeText16063942680760630592" style="display:none">Horrible book! I didn't know Sparks had it in him. I usually love his novels...they're easy, feel-good reads. But this one, ulgh, where do I start?<br /><br />The characters (especially Lexie) were SO annoying through the whole thing. Lexie wasn't willing to sacrifice anything to be with Jeremy...he had to move to Boone Creek, in the middle of nowhere, and do everything else on her terms. Bought the house she wanted, the renovations she wanted, in the city she wanted etc...and meanwhile, she didn't even seem grateful that he gave up everything to be with her (even his best friend who thought he was making a mistake in marrying her so fast). <br /><br />And then to top it off, she kept LYING to him!! She kept sneaking off to see...what's his face (I can't even remember his name...Rodney was it?) and then when Jeremy confronted her about it, not only did she try lying, but she tried manipulating him by turning it around saying it was his fault she had to sneak around! For pete's sake, she was HOLDING HANDS with an ex-boyfriend and then lying about it, I think anyone would be ticked off and suspicious! Not to mention, Rodney and Lexie's best friend, Rachel, were having relationship problems because Rachel thinks Rodney's still in love with Lexie, so what does Lexie do? She tries to "help" by consoling Rodney (ie: holding his hand, going over alone to his place to comfort him and listen) and then lies about it to Jeremy. Cow, cow, cow. Maybe try staying away from Rodney so that him and Rachel could work things out? How Rachel could stand being her friend was beyond me. Nor do I recall Lexie helping Rachel when she fought with Rodney, but she was more than willing to offer a shoulder for Rodney to cry on. <br /><br />Anyways, despite all that, Jeremy still stood by Lexie's side AND gave her the wedding SHE always wanted (of which he wasn't even allowed to invite his entire family in order to keep it small). <br /><br />This story did not make me feel like I was reading about true love, rather I felt like I was reading about blind desperation. <br /><br />Needless to say I will not be reading this book again. It's pretty sad when you can't even cry for the death of the character because you loathed her too much.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16063942680760630592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_608964802" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/608964802" />
    <a title="Kendra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5370908-kendra"><img alt="Kendra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442601375p2/5370908.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/608964802?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kendra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kendra" href="/user/show/5370908-kendra">Kendra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer608964802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8176452531900218201">I hated this book almost from the start. First of all, Jeremy and Lexie meet, have sex, become pregnant, and get engaged...all within six weeks. He doesn't know her middle name, who her friends are, or about a dozen other things you should know about someone when claiming they are the love of your life. He drops his entire life and moves from NYC to Boone Creek to live with Lexie because she refuses to live in NYC. Which isn't a shock considering the rest of the book depicts Lexie as a self-cent</span>
  <span id="freeText8176452531900218201" style="display:none">I hated this book almost from the start. First of all, Jeremy and Lexie meet, have sex, become pregnant, and get engaged...all within six weeks. He doesn't know her middle name, who her friends are, or about a dozen other things you should know about someone when claiming they are the love of your life. He drops his entire life and moves from NYC to Boone Creek to live with Lexie because she refuses to live in NYC. Which isn't a shock considering the rest of the book depicts Lexie as a self-centered brat. She sneaks around behind his back then gets pissed when he calls her on it. She forces him into buying some rundown house that nearly bleeds him dry during renovations. She takes him on an extravagant shopping spree for baby stuff. Oh, and let's not forget the sportscar he'd saved for and lusted after his entire life. I could've handle some of this if Lexie had actually put a dime toward any of this herself. Nope, Jeremy footed the bill for the entire thing.<br /><br />Then this mysterious email pops up and (kind of) threatens to derail everything. But when you find out who's behind the email, you're left with a "are you kidding me?" and not in a good way. Later on Jeremy gets into a fight with his best friend Alvin and ends the friendship--over one fight. While I can't say I condone what Alvin did, his heart was in the right place and he didn't deserve to lose his best friend (although, there was a part of me that thought Alvin was better off with Jeremy). Yet, Lexie has a fight with her bff Rachel and they stay friends. (Lexie gets her way yet again...*insert eye roll*)<br /><br />The ending of At First Sight was typical for a Nicholas Sparks novel in that he simply cannot allow his characters to ride off into the sunset. The ending was not unexpected and didn't leave me with any real emotion for the characters. I'm bound and determined to find one Sparks novel I don't loathe but this one isn't it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8176452531900218201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15534637398672179381">This book just didn't do it for me. I found myself continuing to read it hoping that it would get better. I thought that Sparks was trying to make a book out of nothing...he should have left these characters as they were at the end of True Believer..instead he dragged them along and it ended up being a disaster.<br/><br/>1. I hated the constant fighting...how old are these 2? It's called communication.<br/>2. Alvin...you pig. and lame.<br/>3. The ABS...needless stress and making it seem just too dramatic.<br/>4. Killing</span>
  <span id="freeText15534637398672179381" style="display:none">This book just didn't do it for me. I found myself continuing to read it hoping that it would get better. I thought that Sparks was trying to make a book out of nothing...he should have left these characters as they were at the end of True Believer..instead he dragged them along and it ended up being a disaster.<br /><br />1. I hated the constant fighting...how old are these 2? It's called communication.<br />2. Alvin...you pig. and lame.<br />3. The ABS...needless stress and making it seem just too dramatic.<br />4. Killing Lexie? REALLY!?! After she grew up not having a mother, you do the same thing to her daughter? Really, in my opinion this was a cop-out. I really despeised this ending and it actually made me angry. I'm not saying everyone should live happily ever after but I felt this was more along the lines of shocking rather than fitting with the story.<br /><br />I'm sorry I wasted 2 days on this book. It left nothing but a bad taste in my mouth.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11762297271022457775">I picked this up on a whim at the airport, on my way to see clients in Texas. Up until then the only Sparks book I'd read was Nights in Rodanthe. I think I'd received it as a selection of the month once when I forgot to return the slip. Though I found the character descriptions to be a bit over the top, fantastical as it may have been I did enjoy the story. So much so, that a couple of weeks later I was travling again and I picked up True Believer.<br/><br/>These books certainly aren't challenging my inte</span>
  <span id="freeText11762297271022457775" style="display:none">I picked this up on a whim at the airport, on my way to see clients in Texas. Up until then the only Sparks book I'd read was Nights in Rodanthe. I think I'd received it as a selection of the month once when I forgot to return the slip. Though I found the character descriptions to be a bit over the top, fantastical as it may have been I did enjoy the story. So much so, that a couple of weeks later I was travling again and I picked up True Believer.<br /><br />These books certainly aren't challenging my intellect, but they do cause me to pause and take stock of where I am and what I have. I'm oddly drawn to media which invokes a type of nostalgic revival of poigniant moments of celebration and loss, lately. Maybe I'm entering a mid-life crisis. :)<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38408229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14122595722168948120">I was kind of disappointed with this book. It is about Jeremy, who meets Lexie while on a writing assignment. Soon after, she becomes pregnant, and Jeremy arranges his life to be with Lexie; he moves to her hometown, they purchase a house, and he attempts to get his new life with her in order. I didn't feel much interested in the story, and it seemed kind of predictable. The ending was sad, but it did little to make me feel more connected to this book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Mashal Ahmad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mashal Ahmad" href="/user/show/53070715-mashal-ahmad">Mashal Ahmad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780751541137" href="/book/show/3740116-at-first-sight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53070715-mashal-ahmad?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1944323618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9238022508261215625">I don't know what I was expecting when I started reading Nicholas Spark but it certainly was not this, not because it was astounding but ordinary. Ordinary up to the point of bewilderment. <br/><br/>The writer has described things beautifully, the common problems in being a relationship,trust issues. The anxiety and fear relating with starting a new life, marriage, kids and parenting. Though things and events sometimes seems to get slower and tedious, but I like his way of describing feelings and emotions</span>
  <span id="freeText9238022508261215625" style="display:none">I don't know what I was expecting when I started reading Nicholas Spark but it certainly was not this, not because it was astounding but ordinary. Ordinary up to the point of bewilderment. <br /><br />The writer has described things beautifully, the common problems in being a relationship,trust issues. The anxiety and fear relating with starting a new life, marriage, kids and parenting. Though things and events sometimes seems to get slower and tedious, but I like his way of describing feelings and emotions simply. <br /><br />Despite these I had issues with this novel... I was skeptic through out the whole time, as if there was something wrong, something missing.<br /><br />1. There wasn't any description about how Jeremy Marsh had fallen in love with Lexie.<br />2. There wasn't any logical explanation for the child being his. <br />3. Why the hell he'd had to move down there and she wasn't willing to leave.<br />4. what exactly was the mysterious lights (I know they are called mysterious because they weren't known, but still there has to be something.) <br /><br />As for the ending my instincts were hinting me beforehand, and I wasn't much surprise nor grieved as I don't believe in expecting happy endings all the time, so I was okay with it.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9238022508261215625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/409373105" />
    <a title="Miriam Murcutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2645154-miriam-murcutt"><img alt="Miriam Murcutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442467585p2/2645154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/409373105?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miriam Murcutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miriam Murcutt" href="/user/show/2645154-miriam-murcutt">Miriam Murcutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer409373105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3776648533360732048">At First Sight by Nicholas Sparks<br/><br/>Just like Jeremy and Lexie’s union, this book is really rather a waste of time. It puts you through a relationship from hell with no rewards in sight even if you manage to reach the back cover. This couple’s courtship and marriage is a dispiriting affair peppered with doubts, lies and Lexie-laid emotional minefields that no intelligent man (as Jeremy was portrayed to be) would have tolerated for 10 minutes, never mind 277 pages. Even the poor old baby that the tw</span>
  <span id="freeText3776648533360732048" style="display:none">At First Sight by Nicholas Sparks<br /><br />Just like Jeremy and Lexie’s union, this book is really rather a waste of time. It puts you through a relationship from hell with no rewards in sight even if you manage to reach the back cover. This couple’s courtship and marriage is a dispiriting affair peppered with doubts, lies and Lexie-laid emotional minefields that no intelligent man (as Jeremy was portrayed to be) would have tolerated for 10 minutes, never mind 277 pages. Even the poor old baby that the two managed to conceive during one of their few better moments didn’t escape the misery that casts its shadow over all of this book. Threatened when in the supposed safety and comfort of Lexie’s womb, doomed to be labeled a killer when it pops out, then inhabited by the restless spirit of its dead mother, this baby has been dealt one tough hand. Frankly, we would all have saved a lot of time and effort if Jeremy had stayed put and divorced on the Upper West Side. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3776648533360732048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1395105206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1395105206" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30928416-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457832320p2/30928416.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1395105206?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/30928416-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1395105206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13195715626324934897">Where to begin? This book was atrocious. I felt no connection to the characters at all. I am usually a huge fan of Sparks and his stories - Safe Haven and A Walk To Remember are two of my favorites and they will always be up there when it comes to great love stories. This..? What a load of tripe. First of all, all of the characters are densely stupid. So much so that at times you will feel like you are a Harvard graduate when you're reading it. The mayor is REALLY, REALLY, REALLY involved in eve</span>
  <span id="freeText13195715626324934897" style="display:none">Where to begin? This book was atrocious. I felt no connection to the characters at all. I am usually a huge fan of Sparks and his stories - Safe Haven and A Walk To Remember are two of my favorites and they will always be up there when it comes to great love stories. This..? What a load of tripe. First of all, all of the characters are densely stupid. So much so that at times you will feel like you are a Harvard graduate when you're reading it. The mayor is REALLY, REALLY, REALLY involved in everyone's personal lives. It feels so fake and forced- what mayor knows everything about EVERYONE in his town? That was a little weird. Then there's the fact that Lexie acts like a girl who doesn't know what relationships are. Jeremy voices his concerns with her 'sneaking' around and seeing another guy (even if it's not a romantic type of see- it still isn't right for her to do) and she gets mad at him and makes HIM feel bad. Even though he wasn't the one sneaking around. Go figure. And then when it comes to Jeremy, he's a sex obsessed grown man stuck in a college mind. All he talks about is Lexie and how pretty she is, etc. Though they are having a baby neither one seems really sure that they are invested in the whole process - it's like they don't know what having a baby entails. The relationship felt wrong from the get-go and the whole time I was reading this I was silently rooting for them to separate and find people they are more compatible with. Of course that didn't happen. Then the ending happens and you're just kind of like.."...really?" <br /><br />Basically, this is NOT in Sparks' top five. Or even ten. I used to wonder why all of his books hadn't been made into movies and well, this book gave me the reason. If you're like me and wanted to go back and read all of his earlier novels since you've read his more recent ones, save yourself the trouble and don't even bother. There are just too many other great books that deserve your attention instead. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13195715626324934897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Now Jeremy is living in the tiny town of Boone Creek, North Carolina, engaged to Lexie Darnell, the love of his life, and anticipating the start of their family. But just as his life seems to be settling into a blissful pattern, a mysterious and disturbing e-mail sets off a chain of events that will change the</span>
  <span id="freeText9620713056279016235" style="display:none">There are a few things Jeremy Marsh was sure he’d never do: he’d never leave New York City; never give his heart away after barely surviving one failed marriage; and never become a parent. Now Jeremy is living in the tiny town of Boone Creek, North Carolina, engaged to Lexie Darnell, the love of his life, and anticipating the start of their family. But just as his life seems to be settling into a blissful pattern, a mysterious and disturbing e-mail sets off a chain of events that will change the course of this young couple’s relationship. How well do we really know the ones we love? How do we handle the inevitable doubts, fears concerning parenthood, and stumbling blocks that are sometimes placed in our way? Continuing the story of the young couple introduced in Sparks’s bestselling True Believer, this novel captures all the heartbreak, tension, romance and surprises of those who are newly wed. An astonishing tale about the love between a man and a woman and between a parent and a child, At First Sight is about endings that bring new beginnings . . . tragedies that lead to unexpected joy . . . and, most of all, the magic of everlasting love.<br /><br />For me this was somewhat between 3 and 3.5 star..<br /><br />How can one fall love within a week and that too not knowing other well😂😂😂<br />It can only happen in books and movies..<br /><br />Lexie was bit annoying ..<br />I didn't like her much ..<br /><br />But in end way she sacrificed her life was so emotional..<br /><br />Why can't all love stories have a happy ending???</span>

<div id="review_1801555591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1801555591" />
    <a title="Sheila Myers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28530856-sheila-myers"><img alt="Sheila Myers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391963775p2/28530856.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_757393132" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/757393132?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brianne Durrant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brianne Durrant" href="/user/show/12735265-brianne-durrant">Brianne Durrant</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer757393132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2909250943719440958">I enjoyed “At First Sight”. This book is a great example of how two couples who hardly know each other, manage to make their relationship work. Jeremy, who is a journalist, travels to Boones Creek, South Carolina to write his column on "the Mysterious Lights." As he was doing his column, he met Lexie, who talked about her dead parents and visiting "the Mysterious Lights." In the two weeks he was there, he fell in love with her and decided to propose to her. Instead of coming back to New York wit</span>
  <span id="freeText2909250943719440958" style="display:none">I enjoyed “At First Sight”. This book is a great example of how two couples who hardly know each other, manage to make their relationship work. Jeremy, who is a journalist, travels to Boones Creek, South Carolina to write his column on "the Mysterious Lights." As he was doing his column, he met Lexie, who talked about her dead parents and visiting "the Mysterious Lights." In the two weeks he was there, he fell in love with her and decided to propose to her. Instead of coming back to New York with just a column, he came back with a fiancé as well. This causes a huge conflict between Alvin, Jeremy’s best friend, and him. When Jeremy tells him that he plans to move in with Lexie, he thinks they are moving excessively fast. Then he goes to Boones Creek, where their friendship becomes strained and Alvin does something that risks Jeremy’s friendship and his relationship with Lexie.<br /><br />Before he moved to Boones Creek, Jeremy was more into fashionable attire and loved to do something different each day. When he moved there however, he becomes more relaxed, has less of a humor and wears plaid shirts, which is something he would have never done before.<br /><br />This setting first takes place in New York in the first chapter, and then the rest is Boones Creek, South Carolina, five years in the past. <br /><br />The theme is trust. Throughout this book, Jeremy lacks trust in Lexie and often times, their arguments are centered on lack of trust. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone who loves romance because this book has a lot of it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2909250943719440958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_418623576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/418623576" />
    <a title="Ker Malkin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11088172-ker-malkin"><img alt="Ker Malkin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588747332p2/11088172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/418623576?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ker Malkin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ker Malkin" href="/user/show/11088172-ker-malkin">Ker Malkin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11088172-ker-malkin?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11088172-ker-malkin?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11088172-ker-malkin?shelf=novel">novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer418623576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7389012225165858175">*Edit: First off, I have no idea there was a prequel to this and I absolutely haven't read it yet. So just disregard any complaints or comments I've made below, concerning lack of details. <br/><br/>Originally, my rating for this book was 2.5 stars but I couldn't do that here so I rounded it off. <br/><br/>Nicholas Sparks is a great author, no doubt about that. But here's the thing. His books have exactly the same plot but only with different characters; and twists that would seem to make each of his books distingu</span>
  <span id="freeText7389012225165858175" style="display:none">*Edit: First off, I have no idea there was a prequel to this and I absolutely haven't read it yet. So just disregard any complaints or comments I've made below, concerning lack of details. <br /><br />Originally, my rating for this book was 2.5 stars but I couldn't do that here so I rounded it off. <br /><br />Nicholas Sparks is a great author, no doubt about that. But here's the thing. His books have exactly the same plot but only with different characters; and twists that would seem to make each of his books distinguishable. <br /><br />The first few minutes I read this book, I already knew what would happen. See, that's the problem with Nick's books; this one, at least. It can get too cliche. But meanwhile after reading another few chapters, it was giving me a slight change of what I thought about the forthcoming. It just kept going like that until I was done reading the book. Thus, this read was unput-downable; neither in a bad nor a good way. I was rather desperate to just finish the whole thing. And when I'd arrived to that, I wasn't completely awestruck. But somehow felt a little satisfied.<br /><br /><s>Damn. A nice scene just showed up from Glee.</s><br /><br />The next section could contain some spoilers? xD <br /><br />All my life, this is what I fear the most. To be in Jeremy Marsh's shoes. I would really have loved to read more details about how he met Lexie 'cause this book had failed in that prospect. This was more of retelling what both the characters had felt and how they were handling these trust issues and a couple of "love problems" if you wanna call it, which didn't seem to have a relevance at all to the outcome! Jeremy got divorced from his first marriage because he wasn't capable of bearing a child. With that idea, he can go hit as many girls as he wants. But then after discovering that Lexie (who was probably the last girl he had hooked up with) was pregnant, a miracle, I know, he then made these decisions which includes marrying her and moving in to her town. For the sake of the baby, I supposed. But as the book made it seem so, he was really in love with her and the other way around; which didn't convince me at all. Until their marriage. That was the time when I was finally invested in their characters; but not completely. <br /><br />On the minus side, I thought this book was a little bit all over the place. It felt like some parts shouldn't be there and I completely had no idea what they're supposed to mean and if they even have to do with anything. Those kind of stuffs. For instance, before even arriving to their marriage, Jeremy was receiving these e-mails which ought to break him and his fiancee apart. After dealing with that, the dilemma then felt kinda pointless after reading the resolution part of the plot. Some dialogues too, I thought, were less realistic for my taste. I thought they were cartoon-ish while I was playing the scenes in my mind. I have to say though that the depth of the conflict of the plot wasn't heavy and thick enough. Perhaps not until the labor. There's just something about death that makes you teary-eyed. (No book has ever beaten my sobs in TFiOS yet. Just sayin' ha-ha) Also, along the storyline, some scenarios were getting very stupid and dull. I don't even know if I should give a crap about them or what 'cause the characters were somewhat giving these idiotic lines.<br /><br />But yeah, as I said somewhere above, I was a bit satisfied by the ending. I was surprised (didn't force it, trust me) and I liked the feeling after reading the epilogue. And I loved how the title fitted in the story. Not exactly what I had in mind so overall, good.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1697776005392295443" style="display:none">I made a gaffe where I read this book before the first part. Another gaffe that I kept on reading the books one after the other especially books by Nicholas Sparks which I wanted to read in order and almost did so but with that I kept on missing updating the books and writing the reviews and it kept on going on and the list of books pending for review kept on coming on I kept on dreading updating all in one go so here I am updating them few ones at a time.<br /><br />Coming down to the book since I had forgot to pick the first part of story I felt I missed few things but for me it was a new story and barring few mentions of events from the 1st part I didn't feel that I was missing much and also it was a nice thought little slow read and by this book Nicholas Sparks formula had started to miff me. <div id="review_21737227" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21737227" />
    <a title="Janice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1136840-janice"><img alt="Janice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266355682p2/1136840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21737227?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janice" href="/user/show/1136840-janice">Janice</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21737227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2116455676505212150">The followup to "True Believer", if published together as one story it would have made a great novel. But I liked it and enjoyed reading it. You may need kleenexes to get through it. <br/><br/>There are few things Jeremy Marsh was sure he'd never do: he'd never leave New York City; never give his heart away again after barely surviving one failed marriage; and most of all, never become a parent. Now, Jeremy is living in the tiny town of Boone Creek, North Carolina, married to Lexie Darnell, the love of hi</span>
  <span id="freeText2116455676505212150" style="display:none">The followup to "True Believer", if published together as one story it would have made a great novel. But I liked it and enjoyed reading it. You may need kleenexes to get through it. <br /><br />There are few things Jeremy Marsh was sure he'd never do: he'd never leave New York City; never give his heart away again after barely surviving one failed marriage; and most of all, never become a parent. Now, Jeremy is living in the tiny town of Boone Creek, North Carolina, married to Lexie Darnell, the love of his life, and anticipating the birth of their daughter. But just as his life seems to be settling into a blissful pattern, an unsettling and mysterious message re-opens old wounds and sets off a chain of events that will forever change the course of this young couples marriage</span>

<div id="review_30488710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30488710" />
    <a title="Karen &amp; Gerard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/979933-karen-gerard"><img alt="Karen &amp; Gerard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442619227p2/979933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30488710?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen &amp; Gerard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen &amp; Gerard" href="/user/show/979933-karen-gerard">Karen &amp; Gerard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone contemplating marriage, lovers of romance</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/979933-karen-gerard?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/979933-karen-gerard?shelf=sparks-nicholas">sparks-nicholas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/979933-karen-gerard?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30488710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11719148488228236985">This book is a romance between Jeremy, a successful New York <br/>magazine columnist, who falls in love with Lexie, a country girl, and moves to her neck of the woods away from the city. The author delves into the dynamics of friendship, commitment, marriage, pregnancy and fatherhood. It gave insights into the adjustments involved in entering and maintaining a serious relationship by centering on Jeremy's and Lexie's feelings as their relationship progressed. The ending surprised me so I'd say it is </span>
  <span id="freeText11719148488228236985" style="display:none">This book is a romance between Jeremy, a successful New York <br />magazine columnist, who falls in love with Lexie, a country girl, and moves to her neck of the woods away from the city. The author delves into the dynamics of friendship, commitment, marriage, pregnancy and fatherhood. It gave insights into the adjustments involved in entering and maintaining a serious relationship by centering on Jeremy's and Lexie's feelings as their relationship progressed. The ending surprised me so I'd say it is a good book and recommend it to anyone who likes romance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11719148488228236985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<li class='cover' id='bookCover_15862240'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15862240-the-lucky-one-main-theme"><img alt="The Lucky One (Main Theme): Piano Solo, Sheet" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1355825489l/15862240._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PxjdCAfNSilfBAD1K0BFNSuUekmXt3R1TgSHOphukRmUd7pRNi14fGeOwSkXo6WA+HCgSNH1eo99Db+iCQ0Jeg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yMI1vgrxP6s9VO97LHGYd9rkkRthz8P+LBhPfmZII8hjrVLnOxEN/gXeLqcQknjCCQBLGieNzQQfEXfm9yu7qw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1591799426p3/2345.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10720980456527378788">Nicholas Sparks is one of the world’s most beloved storytellers. All of his books have been <i>New York Times</i> bestsellers, with over 105 million copies sold worldwide, in more than 50 languages, including over 75 million copies in the United States alone.<br/><br/>Sparks wrote one of his best-known stories, <i>The Notebook</i>, over a period of six months at age 28. It was published in 1996 and he followed with the n</span>
  <span id="freeText10720980456527378788" style="display:none">Nicholas Sparks is one of the world’s most beloved storytellers. All of his books have been <i>New York Times</i> bestsellers, with over 105 million copies sold worldwide, in more than 50 languages, including over 75 million copies in the United States alone.<br /><br />Sparks wrote one of his best-known stories, <i>The Notebook</i>, over a period of six months at age 28. It was published in 1996 and he followed with the novels <i>Message in a Bottle</i> (1998), <i>A Walk to Remember</i> (1999), <i>The Rescue</i> (2000), <i>A Bend in the Road</i> (2001), <i>Nights in Rodanthe</i> (2002), <i>The Guardian</i> (2003), <i>The Wedding</i> (2003), <i>True Believer</i> (2005) and its sequel, <i>At First Sight</i> (2005), <i>Dear John</i> (2006), <i>The Choice</i> (2007), <i>The Lucky One</i> (2008), <i>The Last Song</i> (2009), <i>Safe Haven</i> (2010), <i>The Best of Me</i> (2011), <i>The Longest Ride</i> (2013), <i>See Me</i> (2015), <i>Two by Two</i> (2016) and Every Breath (2018) as well as the 2004 non-fiction memoir <i>Three Weeks With My Brother</i>, co-written with his brother Micah. His twenty-first novel, <i>The Return</i>, will be published on September 29, 2020.<br /><br />Film adaptations of Nicholas Sparks novels, including <i>The Choice</i>, <i>The Longest Ride</i>, <i>The Best of Me</i>, <i>Safe Haven</i> (on all of which he served as a producer), <i>The Lucky One</i>, <i>Message in a Bottle</i>, <i>A Walk to Remember</i>,<i> The Notebook</i>, <i>Nights in Rodanthe</i>, <i>Dear John</i> and <i>The Last Song</i>, have had a cumulative worldwide gross of over three-quarters of a billion dollars. <i> The Notebook</i> is also being adapted into a musical, featuring music and lyrics by Ingrid Michaelson. <br /><br />Sparks lives in North Carolina. He contributes to a variety of local and national charities, and is a major contributor to the Creative Writing Program (MFA) at the University of Notre Dame, where he provides scholarships, internships, and a fellowship annually. He co-founded The Epiphany School in New Bern, North Carolina in 2006. As a former full scholarship athlete (he still holds a track and field record at the University of Notre Dame) he also spent four years coaching track and field athletes at the local public high school. In 2009, the team he coached at New Bern High School set a World Junior Indoor Record in the 4x400 meter, in New York. The record still stands. <br /><br />The Nicholas Sparks Foundation, a 501(c)(3) nonprofit committed to improving cultural and international understanding through global education experiences for students of all ages was launched in 2011. Between the foundation, and the personal gifts of the Sparks family, more than $15 million dollars have been distributed to deserving charities, scholarship programs, and projects. Because the Sparks family covers all operational expenses of the foundation, 100% of donations are devoted to programs.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10720980456527378788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

An expert on debunking the supernatural with a regular column in Scientific American, he\'s just made his first appearance on national TV. When he receives a letter from the tiny town of Boone Creek, North Carolina, about ghostly lights that appear in a legend-shrouded cemetery, he can\'t resist driving down to investigate. Here, in this tightly knit community, Lexie Darnell runs the town\'s library, just as her mother did before the accident that left Lexie an orphan. Disappointed by past relationships, including one that lured her away from home, she is sure of one thing: her future is in Boone Creek, close to her grandmother and all the other people she loves. Jeremy expects to spend a quick week in &quot;the sticks&quot; before speeding back to the city. But from the moment he sets eyes on Lexie, he is intrigued and attracted to this beautiful woman who speaks with a soft drawl and confounding honesty. And Lexie, while hesitating to trust this outsider, finds herself thinking of Jeremy more than she cares to admit. Now, if they are to be together, Jeremy Marsh must make a difficult choice: return to the life he knows, or do something he\'s never done before--take a giant leap of faith.
